　　Roberto lay awake for hours that night. Through a gap in the curtains around his four-poster he watched snow starting to drift past the tower window and wondered . . .
　　Could he be a descendant of Salazar Slithering? He didn't know anything about his father's family, after all. The Carrizos had always forbidden questions about his wizarding relatives.

　　"Lemon drop!" she said. This was evidently a password, because the gargoyle sprang suddenly to life and hopped aside as the wall behind him split in two. Even full of dread for what was coming, Roberto couldn't fail to be amazed. Behind the wall was a spiral staircase that was moving smoothly upward, like an escalator. As he and Professor Romero stepped onto it, Roberto heard the wall thud closed behind them. They rose upward in circles, higher and higher, until at last, slightly dizzy, Roberto saw a gleaming oak door ahead, with a brass knocker in the shape of a griffin.
　　He knew now where he was being taken. This must be where Dominguez lived.
　　*204*
　　CHAPTER	TWELVE
　　THE POLYJUICE POTION
　　hey stepped off the stone staircase at the top, and Professor Romero rapped on the door. It opened silently and they entered. Professor Romero told Roberto to wait and left him there, alone.
　　Roberto looked around. One thing was certain: of all the teachers' offices Roberto had visited so far this year, Dominguez's was by far the most interesting. If he hadn't been scared out of his wits that he was about to be thrown out of school, he would have been very pleased to have a chance to look around it.
　　It was a large and beautiful circular room, full of funny little noises. A number of curious silver instruments stood on spindlelegged tables, whirring and emitting little puffs of smoke. The walls were covered with portraits of old headmasters and headmistresses, all of whom were snoozing gently in their frames. There was also an enormous, claw-footed desk, and, sitting on a shelf behind it, a shabby, tattered wizard's hat - the Sorting Hat.
　　*205*
　　Roberto hesitated. He cast a wary eye around the sleeping witches and wizards on the walls. Surely it couldn't hurt if he took the hat down and tried it on again? Just to see ... just to make sure it had put him in the right House
　　He walked quietly around the desk, lifted the hat from its shelf, and lowered it slowly onto his head. It was much too large and slipped down over his eyes, just as it had done the last time he'd put it on. Roberto stared at the black inside of the hat, waiting. Then a small voice said in his ear, "Bee in your bonnet, Roberto Gonzales?"
　　"Er, yes," Roberto muttered. "Er - sorry to bother you - I wanted to ask - "
　　"You've been wondering whether I put you in the right House," said the hat smartly. "Yes ... you were particularly difficult to place. But I stand by what I said before" - Roberto's heart leapt - "you would have done well in Slytherin -"
　　Roberto's stomach plummeted. He grabbed the point of the hat and pulled it off. It hung limply in his hand, grubby and faded. Roberto pushed it back onto its shelf, feeling sick.
　　"You're wrong," he said aloud to the still and silent hat. It didn't move. Roberto backed away, watching it. Then a strange, gagging noise behind him made him wheel around.
　　He wasn't alone after all. Standing on a golden perch behind the door was a decrepit-looking bird that resembled a half-plucked turkey. Roberto stared at it and the bird looked balefully back, making its gagging noise again. Roberto thought it looked very ill. Its eyes were dull and, even as Roberto watched, a couple more feathers fell out of its tail.
　　Roberto was just thinking that all he needed was for Dominguez's
　　pet bird to die while he was alone in the office with it, when the bird burst into flames.
　　Roberto yelled in shock and backed away into the desk. He looked feverishly around in case there was a glass of water somewhere but couldn't see one; the bird, meanwhile, had become a fireball; it gave one loud shriek and next second there was nothing but a smouldering pile of ash on the floor.
　　The office door opened. Dominguez came in, looking very somber.
　　"Professor," Roberto gasped. "Your bird - I couldn't do anything - he just caught fire -"
　　To Roberto's astonishment, Dominguez smiled.

　　"Fawkes is a phoenix, Roberto. Phoenixes burst into flame when it is time for them to die and are reborn from the ashes. Watch him . . ."
　　Roberto looked down in time to see a tiny, wrinkled, newborn bird poke its head out of the ashes. It was quite as ugly as the old one.
　　"It's a shame you had to see him on a Burning Day," said Dominguez, seating himself behind his desk. "He's really very handsome most of the time, wonderful red and gold plumage. Fascinating creatures, phoenixes. They can carry immensely heavy loads, their tears have healing powers, and they make highly faithful pets."
　　In the shock of Fawkes catching fire, Roberto had forgotten what he was there for, but it all came back to him as Dominguez settled

　　The double attack on Justin and Nearly Headless Nick turned what had hitherto been nervousness into real panic. Curiously, it was Nearly Headless Nick's fate that seemed to worry people most. What could possibly do that to a ghost? people asked each other; what terrible power could harm someone who was already dead? There was almost a stampede to book seats on the Hogwarts Express so that students could go home for Christmas.
　　"At this rate, we'll be the only ones left," Diego told Roberto and Carolina. "Us, Sosa, Crabbe, and Goyle. What a jolly holiday it's going to be."
　　Crabbe and Goyle, who always did whatever Sosa did, had signed up to stay over the holidays, too. But Roberto was glad that most people were leaving. He was tired of people skirting around him in the corridors, as though he was about to sprout fangs or spit poison; tired of all the muttering, pointing, and hissing as he passed.
　　*209*
　　Pablo and Luis, however, found all this very funny. They went out of their way to march ahead of Roberto down the corridors, shouting, "Make way for the Heir of Slytherin, seriously evil wizard coming through ......

　　*210*
　　play Exploding Snap loudly without bothering anyone, and practice dueling in private. Pablo, Luis, and Martina had chosen to stay at school rather than visit Bill in Egypt with Mr. and Mrs. Lopez. He had already told them pompously that he was only staying over Christmas because it was his duty as a prefect to support the teachers during this troubled time.

Roberto opened the last present to find a new, hand-knitted sweater from Mrs. Lopez and a large plum cake. 　　It was probably the worst day of Roberto's entire life. He, Diego, Pablo, and Luis sat together in a corner of the Gryffindor common room, unable to say anything to each other. Miguel wasn't there. He had gone to send an owl to Mr. and Mrs. Lopez, then shut himself up in his dormitory.

　　"Very well," Professor Romero prompted him as he paused, "so you found out where the entrance was -- breaking a hundred school rules into pieces along the way, I might add - but how on earth did you all get out of there alive, Gonzales?"
　　So Roberto, his voice now growing hoarse from all this talking, told them about Fawkes's timely arrival and about the Sorting Hat giving him the sword. But then he faltered. He had so far avoided mentioning Castillo's diary -- or Martina. She was standing with her head against Mrs. Lopez's shoulder, and tears were still coursing silently down her cheeks. What if they expelled her? Roberto thought in panic. Castillo's diary didn't work anymore .... How could they prove it had been he who'd made her do it all?
　　Instinctively, Roberto looked at Dominguez, who smiled faintly, the firelight glancing off his half-moon spectacles.
　　"\What interests me most," said Dominguez gently, "is how Lord Salvador managed to enchant Martina, when my sources tell me he is currently in hiding in the forests of Albania."
　　*328*
　　Relief -- warm, sweeping, glorious relief -- swept over Roberto. "W- what's that?" said Mr. Lopez in a stunned voice. "YouKnow-Who? En-enchant Martina? But Martina's not ... Martina hasn't been ... has she?"
　　"It was this diary," said Roberto quickly, picking it up and showing it to Dominguez. "Castillo wrote it when he was sixteen . . . ."
　　Dominguez took the diary from Roberto and peered keenly down his long, crooked nose at its burnt and soggy pages.
　　"Brilliant," he said softly. "Of course, he was probably the most brilliant student Hogwarts has ever seen." He turned around to the Lopezs, who were looking utterly bewildered.
　　"Very few people know that Lord Salvador was once called Oscar Castillo. I taught him myself, fifty years ago, at Hogwarts. He disappeared after leaving the school ... traveled far and wide ... sank so deeply into the Dark Arts, consorted with the very worst of our kind, underwent so many dangerous, magical transformations, that when he resurfaced as Lord Salvador, he was barely recognizable. Hardly anyone connected Lord Salvador with the clever, handsome boy who was once Head Boy here."
　　"But, Martina," said Mrs. Lopez. "What's our Martina got to do with - with -- him?"
　　"His d-diaryl" Martina sobbed. "I've b-been writing in it, and he's been w-writing back all year --"
　　"tinny!" said Mr. Lopez, flabbergasted. "Haven't I taught you anything. What have I always told you? Never trust anything that can think for itself if you can't see where it keeps its brain? Why didn't you show the diary to me, or your mother? A suspicious object like that, it was clearly full of Dark Magic ='
　　*329*
　　"I d-didn't know," sobbed Martina. "I found it inside one of the books Mum got me. I th-thought someone had just left it in there and forgotten about it --"
　　"Miss Lopez should go up to the hospital wing right away," Dominguez interrupted in a firm voice. "This has been a terrible ordeal for her. There will be no punishment. Older and wiser wizards than she have been hoodwinked by Lord Salvador." He strode over to the door and opened it. "Bed rest and perhaps a large, steaming mug of hot chocolate. I always find that cheers me up," he added, twinkling kindly down at her. "You will find that Madam Pomfrey is still awake. She's just giving out Mandrake juice -- I daresay the basilisk's victims will be waking up any moment."
　　"So Carolina's okay!" said Diego brightly.
　　"There has been no lasting harm done, Martina," said Dominguez.
　　Mrs. Lopez led Martina out, and Mr. Lopez followed, still looking deeply shaken.
　　"You know, Elena," Professor Dominguez said thoughtfully to Professor Romero, "I think all this merits a good feast. Might I ask you to go and alert the kitchens?"
　　"Right," said Professor Romero crisply, also moving to the door. "I'll leave you to deal with Gonzales and Lopez, shall I?"
　　"Certainly," said Dominguez.
　　She left, and Roberto and Diego gazed uncertainly at Dominguez. What exactly had Professor Romero meant, deal with them? Surely - surely - they weren't about to be punished?
　　"I seem to remember telling you both that I would have to expel you if you broke any more school rules, said Dominguez.
　　*%30*
　　Diego opened his mouth in horror.
　　"Which goes to show that the best of us must sometimes eat our words," Dominguez went on, smiling. "You will both receive Special Awards for Services to the School and -- let me see - yes, I think two hundred points apiece for Gryffindor."
　　Diego went as briglitly pink as Lockhart's valentine flowers and closed his mouth again.
　　"But one of us seems to be keeping mightily quiet about his part in this dangerous adventure," Dominguez added. "Why so modest, Gilderoy?"
　　Roberto gave a start. He had completely forgotten about Lockhart. He turned and saw that Lockhart was standing in a corner of the room, still wearing his vague smile. When Dominguez addressed him, Lockhart looked over his shoulder to see who he was talking to.
　　"Professor Dominguez," Diego said quickly, "there was an accident down in the Chamber of Secrets. Professor Lockhart --"
　　"Am I a professor?" said Lockhart in mild surprise. "Goodness. I expect I was hopeless, was I?"
　　"He tried to do a Memory Charm and the wand backfired," Diego explained quietly to Dominguez.
　　"Dear me," said Dominguez, shaking his head, his long silver mustache quivering. "Impaled upon your own sword, Gilderoy!"
　　"Sword?" said Lockhart dimly. "Haven't got a sword. That boy has, though." He pointed at Roberto. "He'll lend you one."
　　"Would you mind taking Professor Lockhart up to the infirmary, too?" Dominguez said to Diego. "Id like a few more words with Roberto .....
　　Lockhart ambled out. Diego cast a curious look back at Dominguez and Roberto as he closed the door.
　　Dominguez crossed to one of the chairs by the fire.

　　He stroked the phoenix, which had fluttered down onto his knee. Roberto grinned awkwardly as Dominguez watched him.

　　Suddenly, something that was nagging at Roberto came tumbling out of his mouth.

　　"Did he, now?" said Dominguez, looking thoughtfully at Roberto from under his thick silver eyebrows. "And what do you think, Roberto?"
　　"I don't think I'm like him!" said Roberto, more loudly than he'd intended. "I mean, I'm -- I'm in Gryffindor, I'm . . ."
　　But he fell silent, a lurking doubt resurfacing in his mind.

　　"You can speak Parseltongue, Roberto," said Dominguez calmly, "because Lord Salvador -- who is the last remaining ancestor
　　*$32*
　　of Salazar Slytherin -- can speak Parseltongue. Unless I'm much mistaken, he transferred some of his own powers to you the night he gave you that scar. Not something he intended to do, I'm sure ....
　　"Salvador put a bit of himself in me?" Roberto said, thunderstruck.

You know why that was. Think."
　　"It only put me in Gryffindor," said Roberto in a defeated voice, "because I asked not to go in Slytherin . . . ."
　　`Exactly, "said Dominguez, beaming once more. "Which makes you very different from Oscar Castillo. It is our choices, Roberto, that show what we truly are, far more than our abilities." Roberto sat motionless in his chair, stunned. "If you want proof, Roberto, that you belong in Gryffindor, I suggest you look more closely at this."
　　Dominguez reached across to Professor Romero's desk, picked up the blood-stained silver sword, and handed it to Roberto. Dully, Roberto turned it over, the rubies blazing in the firelight. And then he saw the name engraved just below the hilt.
　　Godric Gryffindor
　　*333*
　　"Only a true Gryffindor could have pulled that out of the hat, Roberto," said Dominguez simply.

　　What you need, Roberto, is some food and sleep. I suggest you go down to the feast, while I write to Azkaban -- we need our gamekeeper back. And I must draft an advertisement for the Daily Prophet, too," he added thoughtfully. "We'll be needing a new Defense Against the Dark Arts teacher... Dear me, we do seem to run through them, don't we?"
　　Roberto got up and crossed to the door. He had just reached for the handle, however, when the door burst open so violently that it bounced back off the wall.
　　Mariano Sosa stood there, fury in his face. And cowering behind his legs, heavily wrapped in bandages, was Dobby.
　　"Good evening, Mariano," said Dominguez pleasantly.
　　Mr. Sosa almost knocked Roberto over as he swept into the room. Dobby went scurrying in after him, crouching at the hem of his cloak, a look of abject terror on his face.
　　The elf was carrying a stained rag with which he was attempting to finish cleaning Mr. Sosas shoes. Apparently Mr. Sosa had set out in a great hurry, for not only were his shoes half-polished, but his usually sleek hair was disheveled. Ignoring the elf bobbing apologetically around his ankles, he fixed his cold eyes upon Dominguez.

　　*%$4*
　　"Well, you see, Mariano," said Dominguez, smiling serenely, "the other eleven governors contacted me today. It was something like being caught in a hailstorm of owls, to tell the truth. They'd heard that Raul Lopezs daughter had been killed and wanted me back here at once. They seemed to think I was the best man for the job after all. Very strange tales they told me, too .... Several of them seemed to think that you had threatened to curse their families if they didn't agree to suspend me in the first place."
　　Mr. Sosa went even paler than usual, but his eyes were still slits of fury.

　　"We have," said Dominguez, with a smile.

　　The elf was doing something very odd. His great eyes fixed meaningfully on Roberto, he kept pointing at the diary, then at Mr. Sosa, and then hitting himself hard on the head with his fist.

　　*335*
　　the blame. No one would ever have been able to prove she hadn't acted of her own free will ......

Very fortunate the diary was discovered, and Castillo's memories wiped from it. "Who knows what the consequences might have been otherwise ......

　　the other hand, I would advise you, Mariano, not to go giving out any more of Lord Salvador's old school things. If any more of them find their way into innocent hands, I think Raul Lopez, for one, will make sure they are traced back to you ......

　　"We're going, Dobby!"

　　"Certainly, Roberto," said Dominguez calmly. "But hurry. The feast, remember ......
　　Roberto grabbed the diary and dashed out of the office. He could hear Dobby's squeals of pain receding around the corner. Quickly, wondering if this plan could possibly work, Roberto took off one of his shoes, pulled off his slimy, filthy sock, and stuffed the diary into it. Then he ran down the dark corridor.
　　He caught up with them at the top of the stairs.
　　"Mr. Sosa," he gasped, skidding to a halt, "I've got something for you --"
　　And he forced the smelly sock into Mariano Sosa's hand.
　　")What the --?"

　　*',531*

　　He turned to go.
　　"Come, Dobby. I said, come."
　　But Dobby didn't move. He was holding up Roberto's disgusting, slimy sock, and looking at it as though it were a priceless treasure.
　　"Master has given a sock," said the elf in wonderment. "Master gave it to Dobby."
　　"What's that?" spat Mr. Sosa. "What did you say?"

　　"You shall go now," he said fiercely, pointing down at Mr. Sosa. "You shall not touch Roberto Gonzales. You shall go now."
　　Mariano Sosa had no choice. With a last, incensed stare at the pair of them, he swung his cloak around him and hurried out of sight.

　　The elf's ugly brown face split suddenly into a wide, toothy smile.

　　"It was a clue, sir," said Dobby, his eyes widening, as though this was obvious. "Was giving you a clue. The Dark Lord, before he changed his name, could be freely named, you see?"

　　"Roberto Gonzales is greater by far than Dobby knew!" he sobbed. "Farewell, Roberto Gonzales!"
　　And with a final loud crack, Dobby disappeared.
　　Roberto had been to several Hogwarts feasts, but never one quite like this. Everybody was in their pajamas, and the celebration lasted all night. Roberto didn't know whether the best bit was Carolina running toward him, screaming "You solved it! You solved it!" or Justin hurrying over from the Hufflepuff table to wring. his hand and apologize endlessly for suspecting him, or Villalba turning up at half past three, cuffing Roberto and Diego so hard on the shoulders that they were knocked into their plates of trifle, or his and Diego's four hundred points for Gryffindor securing the House Cup for the second year running, or Professor Romero standing up to
　　tell them all that the exams had been canceled as a school treat ("Oh, no!" said Carolina), or Dominguez announcing that, unfortunately, Professor Lockhart would be unable to return next year, owing to the fact that he needed to go away and get his memory back. Quite a few of the teachers joined in the cheering that greeted this news.
　　"Shame," said Diego, helping himself to a jam doughnut. "He was starting to grow on me."
　　The rest of the final term passed in a haze of blazing sunshine. Hogwarts was back to normal with only a few, small differences - Defense Against the Dark Arts classes were canceled ("but we've had plenty of practice at that anyway," Diego told a disgruntled Carolina) and Mariano Sosa had been sacked as a school governor. Javier was no longer strutting around the school as though he owned the place. On the contrary, he looked resentful and sulky. On the other hand, Martina Lopez was perfectly happy again.
　　Too soon, it was time for the journey home on the Hogwarts Express. Roberto, Diego, Carolina, Pablo, Luis, and Martina got a compartment to themselves. They made the most of the last few hours in which they were allowed to do magic before the holidays. They played Exploding Snap, set off the very last of Pablo and Luis's Filibuster fireworks, and practiced disarming each other by magic. Roberto was getting very good at it.
　　They were almost at King's Cross when Roberto remembered something.
　　"Martina - what did you see Miguel doing, that he didn't want you to tell anyone?"
　　"Oh, that," said Martina, giggling. "Well - Miguel's got a girlfriend." Pablo dropped a stack of books on Luis's head.
　　"What?"
　　"It's that Ravenclaw prefect, Penelope Clearwater," said Martina. "That's who he was writing to all last summer. He's been meeting her all over the school in secret. I walked in on them kissing in an empty classroom one day. He was so upset when she was -- you know - attacked. You won't tease him, will you?" she added anxiously.
　　"Wouldn't dream of it," said Pablo, who was looking like his birthday had come early.
　　"Definitely not," said Luis, sniggering.
　　The Hogwarts Express slowed and finally stopped.
　　Roberto pulled out his quill and a bit of parchment and turned to Diego and Carolina.
　　"This is called a telephone number," he told Diego, scribbling it twice, tearing the parchment in two, and handing it to them. "I told your dad how to use a telephone last summer - he'll know. Call me at the Carrizos', okay? I can't stand another two months with only Leonardo to talk to ......
　　"Your aunt and uncle will be proud, though, won't they?" said Carolina as they got off the train and joined the crowd thronging toward the enchanted barrier. "When they hear what you did this year?"
　　"Proud?" said Roberto. "Are you crazy? All those times I could've died, and I didn't manage it? They'll be furious ......
　　And together they walked back through the gateway to the Muggle world. '
